Education
B-Title of Presentation: This course has three purposes. First, drawing on the fields of social science and education, this course introduces students to the theories, methods, and paradigmatic frames of social science research to develop the skills that will prepare them to design and conducting of a research projects. Second, the course prepares them to knowledgeably read empirical research reports. Third, this course prepares students to use valid empirical research to support good educational and organizational decision-making. Second, the course prepares them to knowledgeably read empirical research reports. � Research paradigms/philosophies�positivism, phenomenology � Research ethics�humanizing research, human subjects and consent � Approaches to sampling � Research methods�ethnography, surveys, interviews, case studies, action research, observations, single subject study, descriptive and inferential statistics (correlation, regression analysis, tests of significance) � Data analysis � Trustworthiness criteria (threats to validity and reliability) � Exemplars threaded through to illustrate concepts being studied � Using data to make school-based decisions. � Research project including development of research questions, a theoretical or conceptual framework, data collection and analysis, reporting findings.
